| --- | --- | --- |
|  | ‚àÇùí∞‚àÇcj‚Äã(ùêú0)=‚à´‚Ñùk‚àÇh‚Äã(x,ùêú0)‚àÇcj‚Äãp‚Äã(x)‚Äãùüè‚Äã{œï‚Äã(x,ùêú0)‚â•0}‚Äãùëëx+‚à´{x|œï‚Äã(x,ùêú0)=0}h‚Äã(x,ùêú0)‚Äãp‚Äã(x)‚Äã‚àÇœï‚Äã(x,ùêú0)/‚àÇcj‚Äñ‚àáxœï‚Äã(x,ùêú0)‚Äñ2‚Äãùëë‚Ñãk‚àí1‚Äã(x)\displaystyle\frac{\partial\mathcal{U}}{\partial c\_{j}}(\mathbf{c}\_{0})=\int\_{\mathbb{R}^{k}}\frac{\partial h(x,\mathbf{c}\_{0})}{\partial c\_{j}}p(x)\mathbf{1}\{\phi(x,\mathbf{c}\_{0})\geq 0\}\,dx+\int\_{\{x\,|\,\phi(x,\mathbf{c}\_{0})=0\}}h(x,\mathbf{c}\_{0})p(x)\frac{\partial\phi(x,\mathbf{c}\_{0})/\partial c\_{j}}{\|\nabla\_{x}\phi(x,\mathbf{c}\_{0})\|\_{2}}d\mathcal{H}^{k-1}(x) |  |

where ‚Ñãk‚àí1\mathcal{H}^{k-1} is the (k‚àí1)(k-1)-dimensional Hausdorff measure.

###### Proof.

The proof proceeds by analyzing the limit of the difference quotient for ùí∞‚Äã(ùêú)\mathcal{U}(\mathbf{c}) at ùêú0\mathbf{c}\_{0}. Let ùêûj\mathbf{e}\_{j} be the jj-th standard basis vector in ‚Ñùp\mathbb{R}^{p}. The partial derivative is the limit:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | ‚àÇùí∞‚àÇcj‚Äã(ùêú0)=limt‚Üí0ùí∞‚Äã(ùêú0+t‚Äãùêûj)‚àíùí∞‚Äã(ùêú0)t\displaystyle\frac{\partial\mathcal{U}}{\partial c\_{j}}(\mathbf{c}\_{0})=\lim\_{t\to 0}\frac{\mathcal{U}(\mathbf{c}\_{0}+t\mathbf{e}\_{j})-\mathcal{U}(\mathbf{c}\_{0})}{t} |  |

Let g‚Äã(x,ùêú)=h‚Äã(x,ùêú)‚Äãp‚Äã(x)g(x,\mathbf{c})=h(x,\mathbf{c})p(x) and let H‚Äã(z)=ùüè‚Äã{z‚â•0}H(z)=\mathbf{1}\{z\geq 0\} be the Heaviside step function. The difference quotient can be written as:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | 1t‚Äã‚à´‚Ñùk[g‚Äã(x,ùêú0+t‚Äãùêûj)‚ÄãH‚Äã(œï‚Äã(x,ùêú0+t‚Äãùêûj))‚àíg‚Äã(x,ùêú0)‚ÄãH‚Äã(œï‚Äã(x,ùêú0))]‚Äãùëëx\displaystyle\frac{1}{t}\int\_{\mathbb{R}^{k}}\left[g(x,\mathbf{c}\_{0}+t\mathbf{e}\_{j})H(\phi(x,\mathbf{c}\_{0}+t\mathbf{e}\_{j}))-g(x,\mathbf{c}\_{0})H(\phi(x,\mathbf{c}\_{0}))\right]\,dx |  |

We add and subtract g‚Äã(x,ùêú0)‚ÄãH‚Äã(œï‚Äã(x,ùêú0+t‚Äãùêûj))g(x,\mathbf{c}\_{0})H(\phi(x,\mathbf{c}\_{0}+t\mathbf{e}\_{j})) inside the brackets to separate the expression into two parts:

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | Term 1: | ‚à´‚Ñùkg‚Äã(x,ùêú0+t‚Äãùêûj)‚àíg‚Äã(x,ùêú0)t‚ÄãH‚Äã(œï‚Äã(x,ùêú0+t‚Äãùêûj))‚Äãùëëx\displaystyle\int\_{\mathbb{R}^{k}}\frac{g(x,\mathbf{c}\_{0}+t\mathbf{e}\_{j})-g(x,\mathbf{c}\_{0})}{t}H(\phi(x,\mathbf{c}\_{0}+t\mathbf{e}\_{j}))\,dx |  |
|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | Term 2: | ‚à´‚Ñùkg‚Äã(x,ùêú0)‚ÄãH‚Äã(œï‚Äã(x,ùêú0+t‚Äãùêûj))‚àíH‚Äã(œï‚Äã(x,ùêú0))t‚Äãùëëx\displaystyle\int\_{\mathbb{R}^{k}}g(x,\mathbf{c}\_{0})\frac{H(\phi(x,\mathbf{c}\_{0}+t\mathbf{e}\_{j}))-H(\phi(x,\mathbf{c}\_{0}))}{t}\,dx |  |

For the first term, by the Mean Value Theorem, the integrand is equal to ‚àÇg‚Äã(x,ùêú~)‚àÇcj\frac{\partial g(x,\tilde{\mathbf{c}})}{\partial c\_{j}} for some ùêú~\tilde{\mathbf{c}} on the line segment between ùêú0\mathbf{c}\_{0} and ùêú0+t‚Äãùêûj\mathbf{c}\_{0}+t\mathbf{e}\_{j}. By Assumption [A.1](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#A1.Thmassumption1 "Assumption A.1. ‚Ä£ Appendix A Differentiating integrals ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025. Wisse Rutgers acknowledges financial support from the Fundaci√≥n Ram√≥n Areces, the Maria de Maeztu Unit of Excellence CEX2020-001104-M, funded by MCIN/AEI/10.13039/501100011033, and CEMFI.")(2), this is bounded in absolute value by the integrable function Kh‚Äã(x)‚Äãp‚Äã(x)K\_{h}(x)p(x). Therefore, the Dominated Convergence Theorem applies, and Term 1 converges to:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | ‚à´‚Ñùk‚àÇh‚Äã(x,ùêú0)‚àÇcj‚Äãp‚Äã(x)‚Äãùüè‚Äã{œï‚Äã(x,ùêú0)‚â•0}‚Äãùëëx\displaystyle\int\_{\mathbb{R}^{k}}\frac{\partial h(x,\mathbf{c}\_{0})}{\partial c\_{j}}p(x)\mathbf{1}\{\phi(x,\mathbf{c}\_{0})\geq 0\}\,dx |  |

The second term is the derivative of a function ùêú‚Ü¶‚à´{x|œï‚Äã(x,ùêú)‚â•0}h‚Äã(x,ùêú0)‚Äãp‚Äã(x)‚Äãùëëx\mathbf{c}\mapsto\int\_{\{x|\phi(x,\mathbf{c})\geq 0\}}h(x,\mathbf{c}\_{0})p(x)dx. We appeal to the theory of shape derivatives to evaluate this. The conditions in Assumption [A.1](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#A1.Thmassumption1 "Assumption A.1. ‚Ä£ Appendix A Differentiating integrals ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025. Wisse Rutgers acknowledges financial support from the Fundaci√≥n Ram√≥n Areces, the Maria de Maeztu Unit of Excellence CEX2020-001104-M, funded by MCIN/AEI/10.13039/501100011033, and CEMFI.") are sufficient to apply Theorem 4.2 in Delfour and Zol√©sio ([2011](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#bib.bib17)), which guarantees that the derivative exists and is equal to:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | ‚à´{x|œï‚Äã(x,ùêú0)=0}h‚Äã(x,ùêú0)‚Äãp‚Äã(x)‚Äã‚àÇœï‚Äã(x,ùêú0)/‚àÇcj‚Äñ‚àáxœï‚Äã(x,ùêú0)‚Äñ2‚Äãùëë‚Ñãk‚àí1‚Äã(x),\displaystyle\int\_{\{x\,|\,\phi(x,\mathbf{c}\_{0})=0\}}h(x,\mathbf{c}\_{0})p(x)\frac{\partial\phi(x,\mathbf{c}\_{0})/\partial c\_{j}}{\|\nabla\_{x}\phi(x,\mathbf{c}\_{0})\|\_{2}}d\mathcal{H}^{k-1}(x), |  |

thus proving the result.
‚àé

###### Corollary A.1.

Let X=(Y,Z)X=(Y,Z), where Y‚àà‚Ñùk1,Z‚àà‚Ñùk2Y\in\mathbb{R}^{k\_{1}},Z\in\mathbb{R}^{k\_{2}}. Consider ùí∞‚Äã(ùêú)=ùîº‚Äã[h‚Äã(Y,Z,ùêú)‚Äãùüè‚Äã{œï‚Äã(Y,Z,ùêú)‚â•0}]\mathcal{U}(\mathbf{c})=\mathbb{E}[h(Y,Z,\mathbf{c})\mathbf{1}\{\phi(Y,Z,\mathbf{c})\geq 0\}]. Suppose for PZP\_{Z}-almost every zz, the assumptions of Theorem [A.1](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#A1.Thmtheorem1 "Theorem A.1. ‚Ä£ Appendix A Differentiating integrals ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025. Wisse Rutgers acknowledges financial support from the Fundaci√≥n Ram√≥n Areces, the Maria de Maeztu Unit of Excellence CEX2020-001104-M, funded by MCIN/AEI/10.13039/501100011033, and CEMFI.") hold for the conditional expectation over YY. Let gj‚Äã(ùêú|z)g\_{j}(\mathbf{c}|z) be the resulting conditional derivative. If |gj(ùêú|z)||g\_{j}(\mathbf{c}|z)| is dominated by an integrable function K‚Äã(z)K(z), then ùí∞‚Äã(ùêú)\mathcal{U}(\mathbf{c}) is differentiable and

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | ‚àÇùí∞‚Äã(ùêú)‚àÇùêúj=ùîºZ‚Äã[gj‚Äã(ùêú|Z)].\displaystyle\frac{\partial\mathcal{U}(\mathbf{c})}{\partial\mathbf{c}\_{j}}=\mathbb{E}\_{Z}[g\_{j}(\mathbf{c}|Z)]. |  |

###### Proof.

By the law of total expectation, ùí∞‚Äã(ùêú)=ùîºZ‚Äã[ùí∞‚Äã(ùêú|Z)]\mathcal{U}(\mathbf{c})=\mathbb{E}\_{Z}[\mathcal{U}(\mathbf{c}|Z)]. For a.e. zz, ùí∞‚Äã(ùêú|z)\mathcal{U}(\mathbf{c}|z) is differentiable with derivative gj‚Äã(ùêú|z)g\_{j}(\mathbf{c}|z) by Theorem [A.1](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#A1.Thmtheorem1 "Theorem A.1. ‚Ä£ Appendix A Differentiating integrals ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025. Wisse Rutgers acknowledges financial support from the Fundaci√≥n Ram√≥n Areces, the Maria de Maeztu Unit of Excellence CEX2020-001104-M, funded by MCIN/AEI/10.13039/501100011033, and CEMFI."). The domination condition allows us to apply the Differentiated DCT to interchange the derivative and the outer expectation ùîºZ‚Äã[‚ãÖ]\mathbb{E}\_{Z}[\cdot].
‚àé

## Appendix B Derivation of the Marginal Policy Effect

This appendix provides a formal derivation of the Marginal Policy Effect (MPE) discussed in Section [3](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#S3 "3 The Marginal Policy Effect ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025. Wisse Rutgers acknowledges financial support from the Fundaci√≥n Ram√≥n Areces, the Maria de Maeztu Unit of Excellence CEX2020-001104-M, funded by MCIN/AEI/10.13039/501100011033, and CEMFI.") of the main text. We first state the rigorous versions of the assumptions used in the derivation. We then prove a sequence of lemmas and propositions that decompose the MPE into its constituent parts: a direct effect, a competition effect, and a market conduct effect. The proof relies on the result for differentiating integrals over moving domains from Appendix [A](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#A1 "Appendix A Differentiating integrals ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025. Wisse Rutgers acknowledges financial support from the Fundaci√≥n Ram√≥n Areces, the Maria de Maeztu Unit of Excellence CEX2020-001104-M, funded by MCIN/AEI/10.13039/501100011033, and CEMFI.").

Let the space of observable data for an agent be ùíü:=ùí¥√óùíú√ó‚Ñõ√óùí≤\mathcal{D}:=\mathcal{Y}\times\mathcal{A}\times\mathcal{R}\times\mathcal{W}. We assume the baseline policy regime is characterized by a probability measure on ùíü\mathcal{D} that has a density with respect to a product measure Œª\lambda. This density can be factorized as:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | fY|A,W,R‚Äã(y|a,w,r)‚ÄãŒºa‚Äã(r,ùêú0,PR|0)‚ÄãfR|W‚Äã(r|w)‚ÄãfW|0‚Äã(w),\displaystyle f\_{Y|A,W,R}(y|a,w,r)\mu\_{a}(r,\mathbf{c}\_{0},P\_{R|0})f\_{R|W}(r|w)f\_{W|0}(w), |  |

where ùêú0\mathbf{c}\_{0} is the equilibrium parameter vector and PR|0P\_{R|0} is the marginal measure on the report space ‚Ñõ\mathcal{R}, induced by the baseline policy fW|0f\_{W|0}. Its density is fR|0‚Äã(r)=‚à´fR|W‚Äã(r|w)‚ÄãfW|0‚Äã(w)‚Äãùëëwf\_{R|0}(r)=\int f\_{R|W}(r|w)f\_{W|0}(w)dw. We use ùîº0\mathbb{E}\_{0} to denote the expectation with respect to this baseline measure.

A marginal policy reform is a perturbation of the baseline policy distribution fW|0f\_{W|0} in a specific direction. We characterize these directions by a set of score functions.

###### Definition 1 (Policy Score Space).

The space of admissible policy scores, ùíÆW\mathcal{S}\_{W}, is the set of functions sW:ùí≤‚Üí‚Ñùs\_{W}:\mathcal{W}\to\mathbb{R} such that ùîº0‚Äã[sW‚Äã(Wi)]=0\mathbb{E}\_{0}[s\_{W}(W\_{i})]=0 and ùîº0‚Äã[sW2‚Äã(Wi)]<‚àû\mathbb{E}\_{0}[s^{2}\_{W}(W\_{i})]<\infty.

For any given score sW‚ààùíÆWs\_{W}\in\mathcal{S}\_{W}, we can construct a local path of policy distributions indexed by a parameter Œ∏‚àà‚Ñù\theta\in\mathbb{R}. A standard construction that accommodates all scores in ùíÆW\mathcal{S}\_{W} is the linear path:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | fW‚Äã(w|Œ∏,sW)=fW|0‚Äã(w)‚Äã(1+Œ∏‚ÄãsW‚Äã(w))\displaystyle f\_{W}(w|\theta,s\_{W})=f\_{W|0}(w)(1+\theta s\_{W}(w)) |  |

This path is well-defined for Œ∏\theta in a neighborhood of 0. It satisfies fW‚Äã(w|0,sW)=fW|0‚Äã(w)f\_{W}(w|0,s\_{W})=f\_{W|0}(w) and guarantees that the score of the log-likelihood with respect to Œ∏\theta at Œ∏=0\theta=0 is precisely sW‚Äã(w)s\_{W}(w):

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | ‚àÇ‚àÇŒ∏‚Äãlog‚Å°fW‚Äã(w|Œ∏,sW)|Œ∏=0=fW|0‚Äã(w)‚ÄãsW‚Äã(w)fW|0‚Äã(w)=sW‚Äã(w).\displaystyle\frac{\partial}{\partial\theta}\log f\_{W}(w|\theta,s\_{W})\bigg|\_{\theta=0}=\frac{f\_{W|0}(w)s\_{W}(w)}{f\_{W|0}(w)}=s\_{W}(w). |  |

A reform to the policy distribution fWf\_{W} induces a change in the marginal distribution of reports fRf\_{R}. The perturbed report density is given by:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | fR‚Äã(r|Œ∏,sW)=‚à´fR|W‚Äã(r|w)‚ÄãfW‚Äã(w|Œ∏,sW)‚Äãùëëw.\displaystyle f\_{R}(r|\theta,s\_{W})=\int f\_{R|W}(r|w)f\_{W}(w|\theta,s\_{W})dw. |  |

This perturbation of the report distribution also has a well-defined score, sR‚Äã(r)s\_{R}(r), which is characterized by the following result.

###### Lemma B.1 (Induced Score).

The score of the induced report distribution, sR‚Äã(r)=‚àÇ‚àÇŒ∏‚Äãlog‚Å°fR‚Äã(r|Œ∏,sW)|Œ∏=0s\_{R}(r)=\frac{\partial}{\partial\theta}\log f\_{R}(r|\theta,s\_{W})|\_{\theta=0}, is the conditional expectation of the policy score:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | sR‚Äã(r)=ùîº0‚Äã[sW‚Äã(Wi)|Ri=r].\displaystyle s\_{R}(r)=\mathbb{E}\_{0}[s\_{W}(W\_{i})|R\_{i}=r]. |  |

We use ùíÆR\mathcal{S}\_{R} to denote the set of scores sR‚Äã(Ri)s\_{R}(R\_{i}) induced by ùíÆW\mathcal{S}\_{W}.

###### Proof.

By definition, sR‚Äã(r)=fR‚Ä≤‚Äã(r|0)/fR|0‚Äã(r)s\_{R}(r)=f\_{R}^{\prime}(r|0)/f\_{R|0}(r), where the prime denotes the partial derivative with respect to Œ∏\theta at Œ∏=0\theta=0. We have:

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | fR‚Ä≤‚Äã(r|0)\displaystyle f\_{R}^{\prime}(r|0) | =‚à´fR|W‚Äã(r|w)‚ÄãfW‚Ä≤‚Äã(w|0)‚Äãùëëw\displaystyle=\int f\_{R|W}(r|w)f\_{W}^{\prime}(w|0)dw |  |
|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  |  | =‚à´fR|W‚Äã(r|w)‚Äã[sW‚Äã(w)‚ÄãfW|0‚Äã(w)]‚Äãùëëw\displaystyle=\int f\_{R|W}(r|w)[s\_{W}(w)f\_{W|0}(w)]dw |  |
|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  |  | =‚à´fR|W‚Äã(r|w)‚ÄãfW|0‚Äã(w)fR|0‚Äã(r)‚ÄãsW‚Äã(w)‚ÄãfR|0‚Äã(r)‚Äãùëëw\displaystyle=\int\frac{f\_{R|W}(r|w)f\_{W|0}(w)}{f\_{R|0}(r)}s\_{W}(w)f\_{R|0}(r)dw |  |
|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  |  | =fR|0‚Äã(r)‚Äã‚à´fW|R‚Äã(w|r)‚ÄãsW‚Äã(w)‚Äãùëëw=fR|0‚Äã(r)‚Äãùîº0‚Äã[sW‚Äã(Wi)|Ri=r].\displaystyle=f\_{R|0}(r)\int f\_{W|R}(w|r)s\_{W}(w)dw=f\_{R|0}(r)\mathbb{E}\_{0}[s\_{W}(W\_{i})|R\_{i}=r]. |  |

Here the differentiation under the integral is justified because fW‚Äã(w|Œ∏,sW)f\_{W}(w|\theta,s\_{W}) is linear in Œ∏\theta and the DCT can be applied because ùîº0‚Äã[sW2‚Äã(Wi)]<‚àû\mathbb{E}\_{0}[s^{2}\_{W}(W\_{i})]<\infty. Dividing by fR|0‚Äã(r)f\_{R|0}(r) yields the result.
‚àé

###### Assumption B.1 (Marginal Agent Regularity).

For each a‚ààùíúa\in\mathcal{A} define ma‚Äã(r):=ùîº0‚Äã[Yi‚Äã(Wi,a)|Ri=r]m\_{a}(r):=\mathbb{E}\_{0}[Y\_{i}(W\_{i},a)|R\_{i}=r]; we assume

1. 1.

   Report Structure: The report vector can be decomposed as Ri=(Ri,u‚Äãn,Ri,c‚Äão‚Äãn‚Äãt)R\_{i}=(R\_{i,un},R\_{i,cont}), where, conditional on Ri,u‚ÄãnR\_{i,un}, the distribution of Ri,c‚Äão‚Äãn‚ÄãtR\_{i,cont} is absolutely continuous with respect to the Lebesgue measure on ‚Ñùk\mathbb{R}^{k} with a bounded and continuous density function.
2. 2.

   Continuity of Conditional Outcomes: For each allocation a‚ààùíúa\in\mathcal{A} and fixed ru‚Äãnr\_{un}, the conditional mean function rc‚Äão‚Äãn‚Äãt‚Ü¶ma‚Äã(ru‚Äãn,rc‚Äão‚Äãn‚Äãt)r\_{cont}\mapsto m\_{a}(r\_{un},r\_{cont}) is continuous and bounded.

###### Assumption B.2 (Well-Behaved Mechanism).

For any a‚ààùíúa\in\mathcal{A} the allocation probability, Œºa‚Äã(r,ùêú,PR)\mu\_{a}(r,\mathbf{c},P\_{R}), can be decomposed as:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | Œºa‚Äã(r,ùêú,PR)=ha‚Äã(r,ùêú,PR)‚ãÖùüè‚Äã{œïa‚Äã(r,ùêú)‚â•0}\displaystyle\mu\_{a}(r,\mathbf{c},P\_{R})=h\_{a}(r,\mathbf{c},P\_{R})\cdot\mathbf{1}\{\phi\_{a}(r,\mathbf{c})\geq 0\} |  |

where the components satisfy the following conditions at the baseline equilibrium (ùêú0,PR|0)(\mathbf{c}\_{0},P\_{R|0}):

1. 1.

   PRu‚Äãn|0P\_{R\_{u}n|0}-a.s. the functions (rc‚Äão‚Äãn‚Äãt,ùêú)‚Ü¶œïa‚Äã(ru‚Äãn,rc‚Äão‚Äãn‚Äãt,ùêú)(r\_{cont},\mathbf{c})\mapsto\phi\_{a}(r\_{un},r\_{cont},\mathbf{c}), (rc‚Äão‚Äãn‚Äãt,ùêú)‚Ü¶ha‚Äã(ru‚Äãn,rc‚Äão‚Äãn‚Äãt,ùêú,PR|0)(r\_{cont},\mathbf{c})\mapsto h\_{a}(r\_{un},r\_{cont},\mathbf{c},P\_{R|0}) satisfy the conditions laid out in Assumption [A.1](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#A1.Thmassumption1 "Assumption A.1. ‚Ä£ Appendix A Differentiating integrals ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025. Wisse Rutgers acknowledges financial support from the Fundaci√≥n Ram√≥n Areces, the Maria de Maeztu Unit of Excellence CEX2020-001104-M, funded by MCIN/AEI/10.13039/501100011033, and CEMFI.") of Appendix [A](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#A1 "Appendix A Differentiating integrals ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. 2. 2.

   PR|0P\_{R|0}-a.s. the function (ùêú,PR)‚Ü¶ha‚Äã(r,ùêú,PR)(\mathbf{c},P\_{R})\mapsto h\_{a}(r,\mathbf{c},P\_{R}) is Hadamard differentiable with respect to PRP\_{R} at PR|0P\_{R|0} for paths induced by scores sR‚ààùíÆRs\_{R}\in\mathcal{S}\_{R}. Its derivative in the direction sRs\_{R} is a continuous linear functional given by:

   |  |  |  |
   | --- | --- | --- |
   |  | DP‚Äãha‚Äã(r,ùêú,PR|0)‚Äã[sR]=‚à´La,ùêú‚Äã(r,r‚Ä≤)‚ÄãsR‚Äã(r‚Ä≤)‚Äãùëër‚Ä≤\displaystyle D\_{P}h\_{a}(r,\mathbf{c},P\_{R|0})[s\_{R}]=\int L\_{a,\mathbf{c}}(r,r^{\prime})s\_{R}(r^{\prime})dr^{\prime} |  |

   where La,ùêú‚Äã(r,r‚Ä≤)L\_{a,\mathbf{c}}(r,r^{\prime}) is the square-integrable kernel and the mapping ùêú‚Ü¶La,ùêú‚Äã(r,r‚Ä≤)\mathbf{c}\mapsto L\_{a,\mathbf{c}}(r,r^{\prime}) is continuous at ùêú0\mathbf{c}\_{0}.

###### Assumption B.3 (Differentiability of the Market Conduct Rule).

The market conduct rule ùêú‚Äã(PR)\mathbf{c}(P\_{R}) is Hadamard differentiable at the baseline report distribution PR|0P\_{R|0} along the paths induced by scores sRs\_{R}. Its derivative, a continuous linear operator from the space of scores to ‚Ñùp\mathbb{R}^{p}, has the representation:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | ùêú‚Ä≤‚Äã[sR]=‚ü®ùùçc0,sR‚ü©‚ÑãR\displaystyle\mathbf{c}^{\prime}[s\_{R}]=\langle\bm{\psi}\_{c\_{0}},s\_{R}\rangle\_{\mathcal{H}\_{R}} |  |

where ‚ü®‚ãÖ,‚ãÖ‚ü©‚ÑãR\langle\cdot,\cdot\rangle\_{\mathcal{H}\_{R}} is the inner product on a Hilbert space ‚ÑãR\mathcal{H}\_{R} containing the scores, and ùõôc0\bm{\psi}\_{c\_{0}} is the representer of the derivative.

We will split the proof of Theorem [3.1](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#S3.Thmtheorem1 "Theorem 3.1 (The Marginal Policy Effect). ‚Ä£ 3.3 The Equilibrium-Adjusted Outcome ‚Ä£ 3 The Marginal Policy Effect ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025. Wisse Rutgers acknowledges financial support from the Fundaci√≥n Ram√≥n Areces, the Maria de Maeztu Unit of Excellence CEX2020-001104-M, funded by MCIN/AEI/10.13039/501100011033, and CEMFI.") and Corollary [3.1](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#S3.Thmcorollary1 "Corollary 3.1 (The Equilibrium-Adjusted Outcome). ‚Ä£ 3.3 The Equilibrium-Adjusted Outcome ‚Ä£ 3 The Marginal Policy Effect ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. The final result follows from the direct combination of the intermediate results.

###### Lemma B.2 (The Direct Effect).

Suppose Assumption [B.1](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#A2.Thmassumption1 "Assumption B.1 (Marginal Agent Regularity). ‚Ä£ Appendix B Derivation of the Marginal Policy Effect ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025. Wisse Rutgers acknowledges financial support from the Fundaci√≥n Ram√≥n Areces, the Maria de Maeztu Unit of Excellence CEX2020-001104-M, funded by MCIN/AEI/10.13039/501100011033, and CEMFI.") holds.
The direct effect of a policy reform, defined as the welfare impact of perturbing the policy distribution while holding the allocation rule fixed at the baseline (ùêú0,PR|0)(\mathbf{c}\_{0},P\_{R|0}), is given by ùîº0‚Äã[Yi‚ÄãsW‚Äã(Wi)]\mathbb{E}\_{0}[Y\_{i}s\_{W}(W\_{i})].

###### Proof.

The welfare functional for the direct effect is

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | ùí∞direct‚Äã(Œ∏):=‚à´y‚ÄãfY|A,W,R‚ÄãŒºa‚Äã(r,ùêú0,PR|0)‚ÄãfR|W‚ÄãfW‚Äã(w|Œ∏,sW)‚ÄãùëëŒª.\displaystyle\mathcal{U}\_{\text{direct}}(\theta):=\int yf\_{Y|A,W,R}\mu\_{a}(r,\mathbf{c}\_{0},P\_{R|0})f\_{R|W}f\_{W}(w|\theta,s\_{W})d\lambda. |  |

Since Œºa\mu\_{a} is held fixed, this is a standard expectation. The score of the density of the data with respect to Œ∏\theta is simply sW‚Äã(w)s\_{W}(w). The derivative of the expectation is the expectation of the outcome multiplied by the score, which gives ùîº0‚Äã[Yi‚ÄãsW‚Äã(Wi)]\mathbb{E}\_{0}[Y\_{i}s\_{W}(W\_{i})]. The differentiation under the integral is permitted by Assumption [B.1](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#A2.Thmassumption1 "Assumption B.1 (Marginal Agent Regularity). ‚Ä£ Appendix B Derivation of the Marginal Policy Effect ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025. Wisse Rutgers acknowledges financial support from the Fundaci√≥n Ram√≥n Areces, the Maria de Maeztu Unit of Excellence CEX2020-001104-M, funded by MCIN/AEI/10.13039/501100011033, and CEMFI.") which guarantees that the conditional expectation of YiY\_{i} is bounded.
‚àé

Next, we consider the indirect effect. To this end, we define

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | ùí∞part‚Äã(Œ∏):=‚àëa=0K‚à´ma‚Äã(r)‚ÄãŒºa‚Äã(r,ùêú‚Äã(Œ∏,sW),PR|Œ∏,sW)‚ÄãfR|0‚Äã(r)‚Äãùëër\displaystyle\mathcal{U}\_{\text{part}}(\theta):=\sum\_{a=0}^{K}\int m\_{a}(r)\mu\_{a}(r,\mathbf{c}(\theta,s\_{W}),P\_{R|\theta,s\_{W}})f\_{R|0}(r)dr |  |

We define this auxiliary functional, which evolves the market mechanism but holds the population of agents fixed to the baseline distribution, as a tool to isolate the indirect effects via the chain rule.

###### Lemma B.3 (Decomposition of the Indirect Effect).

Suppose Assumptions [B.1](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#A2.Thmassumption1 "Assumption B.1 (Marginal Agent Regularity). ‚Ä£ Appendix B Derivation of the Marginal Policy Effect ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025. Wisse Rutgers acknowledges financial support from the Fundaci√≥n Ram√≥n Areces, the Maria de Maeztu Unit of Excellence CEX2020-001104-M, funded by MCIN/AEI/10.13039/501100011033, and CEMFI.")-[B.3](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#A2.Thmassumption3 "Assumption B.3 (Differentiability of the Market Conduct Rule). ‚Ä£ Appendix B Derivation of the Marginal Policy Effect ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025. Wisse Rutgers acknowledges financial support from the Fundaci√≥n Ram√≥n Areces, the Maria de Maeztu Unit of Excellence CEX2020-001104-M, funded by MCIN/AEI/10.13039/501100011033, and CEMFI.") hold. Then ùí∞part‚Ä≤‚Äã(0)\mathcal{U}^{\prime}\_{\text{part}}(0) exists and is equal to:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | ùí∞part‚Ä≤‚Äã(0)=‚àëa=0Kùîº0‚Äã[ma‚Äã(Ri)‚ÄãLa,ùêú0‚Äã(Ri,Rj)‚ÄãsR‚Äã(Rj)]+‚ü®‚àácùí∞‚Äã(c0,PR|0)‚ãÖùùçc0,sR‚ü©‚ÑãR,\displaystyle\mathcal{U}^{\prime}\_{\text{part}}(0)=\sum\_{a=0}^{K}\mathbb{E}\_{0}[m\_{a}(R\_{i})L\_{a,\mathbf{c}\_{0}}(R\_{i},R\_{j})s\_{R}(R\_{j})]+\langle\nabla\_{c}\mathcal{U}(c\_{0},P\_{R|0})\cdot\bm{\psi}\_{c\_{0}},s\_{R}\rangle\_{\mathcal{H}\_{R}}, |  |

where

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ‚àácùí∞‚Äã(c0,PR|0)=\displaystyle\nabla\_{c}\mathcal{U}(c\_{0},P\_{R|0})= | ‚àëa=0Kùîº0‚Äã[ma‚Äã(Ri)‚Äã‚àáùêúha‚Äã(Ri,ùêú0,PR|0)‚Äãùüè‚Äã{œïa‚Äã(Ri,ùêú0)‚â•0}]+\displaystyle\sum\_{a=0}^{K}\mathbb{E}\_{0}\left[m\_{a}(R\_{i})\nabla\_{\mathbf{c}}h\_{a}(R\_{i},\mathbf{c}\_{0},P\_{R|0})\mathbf{1}\{\phi\_{a}(R\_{i},\mathbf{c}\_{0})\geq 0\}\right]+ |  |
|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  |  | ‚àëa=0Kùîº0‚Äã[ùîº0‚Äã[ma‚Äã(Ri)‚Äãha‚Äã(Ri,ùêú0,PR|0)‚Äã‚àáùêúœïa‚Äã(Ri,ùêú0)‚à£Ri,u‚Äãn,œïa‚Äã(Ri,ùêú0)=0]‚Äãfœïa‚Äã(0‚à£Ri,u‚Äãn)],\displaystyle\sum\_{a=0}^{K}\mathbb{E}\_{0}\left[\mathbb{E}\_{0}\left[m\_{a}(R\_{i})h\_{a}(R\_{i},\mathbf{c}\_{0},P\_{R|0})\nabla\_{\mathbf{c}}\phi\_{a}(R\_{i},\mathbf{c}\_{0})\mid R\_{i,un},\phi\_{a}(R\_{i},\mathbf{c}\_{0})=0\right]f\_{\phi\_{a}}(0\mid R\_{i,un})\right], |  |

and fœïa‚Äã(0‚à£ru‚Äãn)f\_{\phi\_{a}}(0\mid r\_{un}) is the conditional density of œïa‚Äã(Ri,ùêú0)\phi\_{a}(R\_{i},\mathbf{c}\_{0}) given Ri,u‚Äãn=ru‚ÄãnR\_{i,un}=r\_{un}.

###### Proof.

The derivative of ùí∞part‚Äã(Œ∏)\mathcal{U}\_{\text{part}}(\theta) at Œ∏=0\theta=0 can be found by applying the chain rule to the underlying functional ùí∞‚Äã(ùêú,PR)=‚àëa‚à´ma‚Äã(r)‚ÄãŒºa‚Äã(r,ùêú,PR)‚ÄãfR|0‚Äã(r)‚Äãùëër\mathcal{U}(\mathbf{c},P\_{R})=\sum\_{a}\int m\_{a}(r)\mu\_{a}(r,\mathbf{c},P\_{R})f\_{R|0}(r)dr. The derivative is the sum of the partial derivatives with respect to each argument, evaluated along the path of the reform:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | ùí∞part‚Ä≤‚Äã(0)=DP‚Äãùí∞‚Äã(ùêú0,PR|0)‚Äã[sR]‚èüCompetition Effect+‚àácùí∞‚Äã(ùêú0,PR|0)‚ãÖùêú‚Ä≤‚Äã[sR]‚èüMarket Conduct Effect.\displaystyle\mathcal{U}^{\prime}\_{\text{part}}(0)=\underbrace{D\_{P}\mathcal{U}(\mathbf{c}\_{0},P\_{R|0})[s\_{R}]}\_{\text{Competition Effect}}+\underbrace{\nabla\_{c}\mathcal{U}(\mathbf{c}\_{0},P\_{R|0})\cdot\mathbf{c}^{\prime}[s\_{R}]}\_{\text{Market Conduct Effect}}. |  |

The first term, the Competition Effect, is the functional derivative with respect to PRP\_{R} in the direction of the induced score sRs\_{R}. Using Assumption [B.2](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#A2.Thmassumption2 "Assumption B.2 (Well-Behaved Mechanism). ‚Ä£ Appendix B Derivation of the Marginal Policy Effect ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025. Wisse Rutgers acknowledges financial support from the Fundaci√≥n Ram√≥n Areces, the Maria de Maeztu Unit of Excellence CEX2020-001104-M, funded by MCIN/AEI/10.13039/501100011033, and CEMFI."), it is:

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | DP‚Äãùí∞‚Äã(ùêú0,PR|0)‚Äã[sR]\displaystyle D\_{P}\mathcal{U}(\mathbf{c}\_{0},P\_{R|0})[s\_{R}] | =‚àëaùîº0‚Äã[ma‚Äã(Ri)‚ÄãDP‚ÄãŒºa‚Äã(Ri,ùêú0,PR|0)‚Äã[sR]]\displaystyle=\sum\_{a}\mathbb{E}\_{0}[m\_{a}(R\_{i})D\_{P}\mu\_{a}(R\_{i},\mathbf{c}\_{0},P\_{R|0})[s\_{R}]] |  |
|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  |  | =‚àëaùîº0‚Äã[ma‚Äã(Ri)‚Äãùüè‚Äã{œïa‚Äã(Ri,ùêú0)‚â•0}‚ÄãDP‚Äãha‚Äã(Ri,ùêú0,PR|0)‚Äã[sR]]\displaystyle=\sum\_{a}\mathbb{E}\_{0}[m\_{a}(R\_{i})\mathbf{1}\{\phi\_{a}(R\_{i},\mathbf{c}\_{0})\geq 0\}D\_{P}h\_{a}(R\_{i},\mathbf{c}\_{0},P\_{R|0})[s\_{R}]] |  |
|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  |  | =‚àëaùîº0‚Äã[ma‚Äã(Ri)‚Äã‚à´La,ùêú0‚Äã(Ri,r‚Ä≤)‚ÄãsR‚Äã(r‚Ä≤)‚Äãùëër‚Ä≤]\displaystyle=\sum\_{a}\mathbb{E}\_{0}\left[m\_{a}(R\_{i})\int L\_{a,\mathbf{c}\_{0}}(R\_{i},r^{\prime})s\_{R}(r^{\prime})dr^{\prime}\right] |  |
|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  |  | =‚àëaùîº0‚Äã[ma‚Äã(Ri)‚ÄãLa,ùêú0‚Äã(Ri,Rj)‚ÄãsR‚Äã(Rj)].\displaystyle=\sum\_{a}\mathbb{E}\_{0}[m\_{a}(R\_{i})L\_{a,\mathbf{c}\_{0}}(R\_{i},R\_{j})s\_{R}(R\_{j})]. |  |

The second term is the Market Conduct Effect. The gradient ‚àácùí∞‚Äã(ùêú0,PR|0)\nabla\_{c}\mathcal{U}(\mathbf{c}\_{0},P\_{R|0}) is derived by applying Corollary [A.1](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#A1.Thmcorollary1 "Corollary A.1. ‚Ä£ Appendix A Differentiating integrals ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025. Wisse Rutgers acknowledges financial support from the Fundaci√≥n Ram√≥n Areces, the Maria de Maeztu Unit of Excellence CEX2020-001104-M, funded by MCIN/AEI/10.13039/501100011033, and CEMFI.") from Appendix [A](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#A1 "Appendix A Differentiating integrals ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025. Wisse Rutgers acknowledges financial support from the Fundaci√≥n Ram√≥n Areces, the Maria de Maeztu Unit of Excellence CEX2020-001104-M, funded by MCIN/AEI/10.13039/501100011033, and CEMFI."), yielding the expression in the lemma statement. Combining this with the derivative of the market conduct rule from Assumption [B.3](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#A2.Thmassumption3 "Assumption B.3 (Differentiability of the Market Conduct Rule). ‚Ä£ Appendix B Derivation of the Marginal Policy Effect ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025. Wisse Rutgers acknowledges financial support from the Fundaci√≥n Ram√≥n Areces, the Maria de Maeztu Unit of Excellence CEX2020-001104-M, funded by MCIN/AEI/10.13039/501100011033, and CEMFI."), ùêú‚Ä≤‚Äã[sR]=‚ü®ùùçc0,sR‚ü©‚ÑãR\mathbf{c}^{\prime}[s\_{R}]=\langle\bm{\psi}\_{c\_{0}},s\_{R}\rangle\_{\mathcal{H}\_{R}}, gives the second part of the result. Summing the two effects proves the lemma.
‚àé

###### Lemma B.4 (Decomposition of the MPE).

Suppose Assumptions [B.1](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#A2.Thmassumption1 "Assumption B.1 (Marginal Agent Regularity). ‚Ä£ Appendix B Derivation of the Marginal Policy Effect ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025. Wisse Rutgers acknowledges financial support from the Fundaci√≥n Ram√≥n Areces, the Maria de Maeztu Unit of Excellence CEX2020-001104-M, funded by MCIN/AEI/10.13039/501100011033, and CEMFI.")-[B.3](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#A2.Thmassumption3 "Assumption B.3 (Differentiability of the Market Conduct Rule). ‚Ä£ Appendix B Derivation of the Marginal Policy Effect ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025. Wisse Rutgers acknowledges financial support from the Fundaci√≥n Ram√≥n Areces, the Maria de Maeztu Unit of Excellence CEX2020-001104-M, funded by MCIN/AEI/10.13039/501100011033, and CEMFI.") hold; then the total MPE can be decomposed into a direct effect and an indirect equilibrium effect:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | ùí∞‚Ä≤‚Äã(0)=ùîº0‚Äã[Yi‚ÄãsW‚Äã(Wi)]+ùí∞part‚Ä≤‚Äã(0).\displaystyle\mathcal{U}^{\prime}(0)=\mathbb{E}\_{0}[Y\_{i}s\_{W}(W\_{i})]+\mathcal{U}^{\prime}\_{\text{part}}(0). |  |

###### Proof.

We analyze the difference quotient for ùí∞‚Äã(Œ∏)\mathcal{U}(\theta). Let Œºa‚Äã(Œ∏)=Œºa‚Äã(r,ùêú‚Äã(Œ∏),PR|Œ∏)\mu\_{a}(\theta)=\mu\_{a}(r,\mathbf{c}(\theta),P\_{R|\theta}) and Œºa‚Äã(0)=Œºa‚Äã(r,ùêú0,PR|0)\mu\_{a}(0)=\mu\_{a}(r,\mathbf{c}\_{0},P\_{R|0}). The difference quotient is:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | ùí∞‚Äã(Œ∏)‚àíùí∞‚Äã(0)Œ∏=1Œ∏‚Äã‚à´y‚ÄãfY|A,W,R‚Äã[Œºa‚Äã(Œ∏)‚ÄãfR|W‚ÄãfW‚Äã(Œ∏)‚àíŒºa‚Äã(0)‚ÄãfR|W‚ÄãfW‚Äã(0)]‚ÄãùëëŒª\displaystyle\frac{\mathcal{U}(\theta)-\mathcal{U}(0)}{\theta}=\frac{1}{\theta}\int yf\_{Y|A,W,R}\left[\mu\_{a}(\theta)f\_{R|W}f\_{W}(\theta)-\mu\_{a}(0)f\_{R|W}f\_{W}(0)\right]d\lambda |  |

We decompose the term in the brackets by adding and subtracting Œºa‚Äã(0)‚ÄãfR|W‚ÄãfW‚Äã(Œ∏)\mu\_{a}(0)f\_{R|W}f\_{W}(\theta):

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | 1Œ∏‚Äã‚à´y‚ÄãfY|A,W,R‚Äã[(Œºa‚Äã(Œ∏)‚àíŒºa‚Äã(0))‚ÄãfR|W‚ÄãfW‚Äã(Œ∏)+Œºa‚Äã(0)‚ÄãfR|W‚Äã(fW‚Äã(Œ∏)‚àífW‚Äã(0))]‚ÄãùëëŒª\displaystyle\frac{1}{\theta}\int yf\_{Y|A,W,R}\left[(\mu\_{a}(\theta)-\mu\_{a}(0))f\_{R|W}f\_{W}(\theta)+\mu\_{a}(0)f\_{R|W}(f\_{W}(\theta)-f\_{W}(0))\right]d\lambda |  |

The second term in this sum corresponds to the direct effect. As Œ∏‚Üí0\theta\to 0, its limit is ùîº0‚Äã[Yi‚ÄãsW‚Äã(Wi)]\mathbb{E}\_{0}[Y\_{i}s\_{W}(W\_{i})] by Lemma [B.2](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#A2.Thmlemma2 "Lemma B.2 (The Direct Effect). ‚Ä£ Appendix B Derivation of the Marginal Policy Effect ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025. Wisse Rutgers acknowledges financial support from the Fundaci√≥n Ram√≥n Areces, the Maria de Maeztu Unit of Excellence CEX2020-001104-M, funded by MCIN/AEI/10.13039/501100011033, and CEMFI."). We now focus on the first term, which captures the indirect effect:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | Indirect Term=1Œ∏‚Äã‚à´y‚ÄãfY|A,W,R‚Äã(Œºa‚Äã(Œ∏)‚àíŒºa‚Äã(0))‚ÄãfR|W‚ÄãfW‚Äã(Œ∏)‚ÄãùëëŒª\displaystyle\text{Indirect Term}=\frac{1}{\theta}\int yf\_{Y|A,W,R}(\mu\_{a}(\theta)-\mu\_{a}(0))f\_{R|W}f\_{W}(\theta)d\lambda |  |

We further decompose this by writing fW‚Äã(Œ∏)=fW‚Äã(0)+(fW‚Äã(Œ∏)‚àífW‚Äã(0))f\_{W}(\theta)=f\_{W}(0)+(f\_{W}(\theta)-f\_{W}(0)):

|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | Indirect Term | =1Œ∏‚Äã‚à´y‚ÄãfY|A,W,R‚Äã(Œºa‚Äã(Œ∏)‚àíŒºa‚Äã(0))‚ÄãfR|W‚ÄãfW‚Äã(0)‚ÄãùëëŒª\displaystyle=\frac{1}{\theta}\int yf\_{Y|A,W,R}(\mu\_{a}(\theta)-\mu\_{a}(0))f\_{R|W}f\_{W}(0)d\lambda\qquad | (A)\displaystyle(A) |  |
|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  |  | +‚à´y‚ÄãfY|A,W,R‚Äã(Œºa‚Äã(Œ∏)‚àíŒºa‚Äã(0))‚ÄãfR|W‚ÄãfW‚Äã(Œ∏)‚àífW‚Äã(0)Œ∏‚ÄãùëëŒª\displaystyle+\int yf\_{Y|A,W,R}(\mu\_{a}(\theta)-\mu\_{a}(0))f\_{R|W}\frac{f\_{W}(\theta)-f\_{W}(0)}{\theta}d\lambda\qquad | (B)\displaystyle(B) |  |

The second part, Term (B), is negligible. As Œ∏‚Üí0\theta\to 0, the factor (Œºa‚Äã(Œ∏)‚àíŒºa‚Äã(0))(\mu\_{a}(\theta)-\mu\_{a}(0)) converges to 0 due to the continuity of the mechanism and market conduct rule. The other factor, fW‚Äã(Œ∏)‚àífW‚Äã(0)Œ∏\frac{f\_{W}(\theta)-f\_{W}(0)}{\theta}, converges to sW‚Äã(w)‚ÄãfW|0‚Äã(w)s\_{W}(w)f\_{W|0}(w). Thus, the entire integrand converges pointwise to 0. The Dominated Convergence Theorem (justified by our assumptions) implies the integral of this term converges to 0.

The first part, Term (A), is the difference quotient for ùí∞part‚Äã(Œ∏)\mathcal{U}\_{\text{part}}(\theta). By integrating over yy and ww with the baseline policy fW‚Äã(0)f\_{W}(0), the expression becomes:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | Term (A)=1Œ∏‚Äã(‚à´ma‚Äã(r)‚ÄãŒºa‚Äã(Œ∏)‚ÄãfR|0‚Äã(r)‚Äãùëër‚àí‚à´ma‚Äã(r)‚ÄãŒºa‚Äã(0)‚ÄãfR|0‚Äã(r)‚Äãùëër)=ùí∞part‚Äã(Œ∏)‚àíùí∞part‚Äã(0)Œ∏\displaystyle\text{Term (A)}=\frac{1}{\theta}\left(\int m\_{a}(r)\mu\_{a}(\theta)f\_{R|0}(r)dr-\int m\_{a}(r)\mu\_{a}(0)f\_{R|0}(r)dr\right)=\frac{\mathcal{U}\_{\text{part}}(\theta)-\mathcal{U}\_{\text{part}}(0)}{\theta} |  |

Taking the limit as Œ∏‚Üí0\theta\to 0 for all terms, we find that ùí∞‚Ä≤‚Äã(0)\mathcal{U}^{\prime}(0) is the sum of the direct effect and ùí∞part‚Ä≤‚Äã(0)\mathcal{U}^{\prime}\_{\text{part}}(0), which proves the result.
‚àé

###### Lemma B.5 (Identification).

Suppose Assumptions [B.1](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#A2.Thmassumption1 "Assumption B.1 (Marginal Agent Regularity). ‚Ä£ Appendix B Derivation of the Marginal Policy Effect ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025. Wisse Rutgers acknowledges financial support from the Fundaci√≥n Ram√≥n Areces, the Maria de Maeztu Unit of Excellence CEX2020-001104-M, funded by MCIN/AEI/10.13039/501100011033, and CEMFI.")-[B.3](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#A2.Thmassumption3 "Assumption B.3 (Differentiability of the Market Conduct Rule). ‚Ä£ Appendix B Derivation of the Marginal Policy Effect ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025. Wisse Rutgers acknowledges financial support from the Fundaci√≥n Ram√≥n Areces, the Maria de Maeztu Unit of Excellence CEX2020-001104-M, funded by MCIN/AEI/10.13039/501100011033, and CEMFI.") hold. Also, suppose ùîº0‚Äã[1ha‚Äã(Ri,ùêú0,PR|0)]<‚àû\mathbb{E}\_{0}\left[\frac{1}{h\_{a}(R\_{i},\mathbf{c}\_{0},P\_{R|0})}\right]<\infty and ùîº0‚Äã[(‚Äñ‚àáùêúh‚Äã(Ri,ùêú0,PR|0)‚Äñ2ha‚Äã(Ri,ùêú0,PR|0))2]<‚àû\mathbb{E}\_{0}\left[\left(\frac{\|\nabla\_{\mathbf{c}}h(R\_{i},\mathbf{c}\_{0},P\_{R|0})\|\_{2}}{h\_{a}(R\_{i},\mathbf{c}\_{0},P\_{R|0})}\right)^{2}\right]<\infty Then the MPE is identified

###### Proof.

To show identification, we must express the components of the MPE as expectations over the observed data distribution. The core of the argument is an inverse weighting identity that allows us to replace the unobserved ma‚Äã(Ri)m\_{a}(R\_{i}) with the observed outcome YiY\_{i}. For any sufficiently regular function g‚Äã(a,r,r‚Ä≤)g(a,r,r^{\prime}), the following identity holds:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | ‚àëa=0Kùîº0‚Äã[ma‚Äã(Ri)‚Äãg‚Äã(a,Ri,Rj)‚ÄãŒºa‚Äã(Ri,ùêú0,PR|0)]=ùîº0‚Äã[Yi‚Äãg‚Äã(Ai,Ri,Rj)].\displaystyle\sum\_{a=0}^{K}\mathbb{E}\_{0}[m\_{a}(R\_{i})g(a,R\_{i},R\_{j})\mu\_{a}(R\_{i},\mathbf{c}\_{0},P\_{R|0})]=\mathbb{E}\_{0}[Y\_{i}g(A\_{i},R\_{i},R\_{j})]. |  |

To see this, we apply the law of iterated expectations to the right-hand side, conditioning first on (Ai,Ri,Rj)(A\_{i},R\_{i},R\_{j}):

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ùîº0‚Äã[Yi‚Äãg‚Äã(Ai,Ri,Rj)]\displaystyle\mathbb{E}\_{0}[Y\_{i}g(A\_{i},R\_{i},R\_{j})] | =ùîº0‚Äã[ùîº0‚Äã[Yi|Ai,Ri,Rj]‚Äãg‚Äã(Ai,Ri,Rj)]\displaystyle=\mathbb{E}\_{0}[\mathbb{E}\_{0}[Y\_{i}|A\_{i},R\_{i},R\_{j}]g(A\_{i},R\_{i},R\_{j})] |  |
|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  |  | =ùîº0‚Äã[mAi‚Äã(Ri)‚Äãg‚Äã(Ai,Ri,Rj)]\displaystyle=\mathbb{E}\_{0}[m\_{A\_{i}}(R\_{i})g(A\_{i},R\_{i},R\_{j})] |  |
|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  |  | =‚àëa=0Kùîº0‚Äã[ma‚Äã(Ri)‚Äãg‚Äã(a,Ri,Rj)‚Äãùüè‚Äã{Ai=a}]\displaystyle=\sum\_{a=0}^{K}\mathbb{E}\_{0}[m\_{a}(R\_{i})g(a,R\_{i},R\_{j})\mathbf{1}\{A\_{i}=a\}] |  |
|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  |  | =‚àëa=0Kùîº0‚Äã[ma‚Äã(Ri)‚Äãg‚Äã(a,Ri,Rj)‚Äã‚Ñô‚Äã(Ai=a|Ri,Rj)],\displaystyle=\sum\_{a=0}^{K}\mathbb{E}\_{0}[m\_{a}(R\_{i})g(a,R\_{i},R\_{j})\mathbb{P}(A\_{i}=a|R\_{i},R\_{j})], |  |

where the second line follows from the definition of mam\_{a} and the fact that YiY\_{i} is independent of RjR\_{j} conditional on (Ai,Ri)(A\_{i},R\_{i}). Since ‚Ñô‚Äã(Ai=a|Ri,Rj)=Œºa‚Äã(Ri,ùêú0,PR|0)\mathbb{P}(A\_{i}=a|R\_{i},R\_{j})=\mu\_{a}(R\_{i},\mathbf{c}\_{0},P\_{R|0}), the identity is established. The moment conditions in the Lemma statement ensure these expectations are well-defined.

We now apply this identity to the two terms.

1. Competition Effect Term:
Let g‚Äã(a,Ri,Rj)=La,ùêú0‚Äã(Ri,Rj)ha‚Äã(Ri,ùêú0,PR|0)‚ÄãsR‚Äã(Rj)g(a,R\_{i},R\_{j})=\frac{L\_{a,\mathbf{c}\_{0}}(R\_{i},R\_{j})}{h\_{a}(R\_{i},\mathbf{c}\_{0},P\_{R|0})}s\_{R}(R\_{j}). The term is:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | ‚àëa=0Kùîº0‚Äã[ma‚Äã(Ri)‚ÄãLa,ùêú0‚Äã(Ri,Rj)‚ÄãsR‚Äã(Rj)].\displaystyle\sum\_{a=0}^{K}\mathbb{E}\_{0}[m\_{a}(R\_{i})L\_{a,\mathbf{c}\_{0}}(R\_{i},R\_{j})s\_{R}(R\_{j})]. |  |

Note that La,ùêú0‚Äã(Ri,Rj)L\_{a,\mathbf{c}\_{0}}(R\_{i},R\_{j}) must be zero if agent ii is ineligible (œïa‚Äã(Ri,ùêú0)<0\phi\_{a}(R\_{i},\mathbf{c}\_{0})<0), as their allocation cannot be affected by others. Thus, we can write the term as:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | ‚àëa=0Kùîº0‚Äã[ma‚Äã(Ri)‚ÄãLa,ùêú0‚Äã(Ri,Rj)ha‚Äã(Ri,ùêú0,PR|0)‚ÄãŒºa‚Äã(Ri,ùêú0,PR|0)‚ÄãsR‚Äã(Rj)].\displaystyle\sum\_{a=0}^{K}\mathbb{E}\_{0}\left[m\_{a}(R\_{i})\frac{L\_{a,\mathbf{c}\_{0}}(R\_{i},R\_{j})}{h\_{a}(R\_{i},\mathbf{c}\_{0},P\_{R|0})}\mu\_{a}(R\_{i},\mathbf{c}\_{0},P\_{R|0})s\_{R}(R\_{j})\right]. |  |

Using our identity, this is equal to ùîº0‚Äã[Yi‚ÄãLAi,ùêú0‚Äã(Ri,Rj)hAi‚Äã(Ri,ùêú0,PR|0)‚ÄãsR‚Äã(Rj)]\mathbb{E}\_{0}\left[Y\_{i}\frac{L\_{A\_{i},\mathbf{c}\_{0}}(R\_{i},R\_{j})}{h\_{A\_{i}}(R\_{i},\mathbf{c}\_{0},P\_{R|0})}s\_{R}(R\_{j})\right], which simplifies to ùîº0‚Äã[Œ≥‚Äã(Rj)‚ÄãsW‚Äã(Wj)]\mathbb{E}\_{0}[\gamma(R\_{j})s\_{W}(W\_{j})]. The assumption ùîº0‚Äã[1/ha]<‚àû\mathbb{E}\_{0}[1/h\_{a}]<\infty ensures this expression is well-defined.

2. Inframarginal Market Conduct Term:
Let g‚Äã(a,Ri,Rj)=‚àáùêúha‚Äã(Ri,ùêú0,PR|0)ha‚Äã(Ri,ùêú0,PR|0)g(a,R\_{i},R\_{j})=\frac{\nabla\_{\mathbf{c}}h\_{a}(R\_{i},\mathbf{c}\_{0},P\_{R|0})}{h\_{a}(R\_{i},\mathbf{c}\_{0},P\_{R|0})}. The term is:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | ‚àëa=0Kùîº0‚Äã[ma‚Äã(Ri)‚Äã‚àáùêúha‚Äã(Ri,ùêú0,PR|0)‚Äãùüè‚Äã{œïa‚Äã(Ri,ùêú0)‚â•0}].\displaystyle\sum\_{a=0}^{K}\mathbb{E}\_{0}[m\_{a}(R\_{i})\nabla\_{\mathbf{c}}h\_{a}(R\_{i},\mathbf{c}\_{0},P\_{R|0})\mathbf{1}\{\phi\_{a}(R\_{i},\mathbf{c}\_{0})\geq 0\}]. |  |

Replacing the indicator with Œºa/ha\mu\_{a}/h\_{a} and applying the identity yields the identified expression:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | ùîº0‚Äã[Yi‚Äã‚àáùêúhAi‚Äã(Ri,ùêú0,PR|0)hAi‚Äã(Ri,ùêú0,PR|0)].\displaystyle\mathbb{E}\_{0}\left[Y\_{i}\frac{\nabla\_{\mathbf{c}}h\_{A\_{i}}(R\_{i},\mathbf{c}\_{0},P\_{R|0})}{h\_{A\_{i}}(R\_{i},\mathbf{c}\_{0},P\_{R|0})}\right]. |  |

The assumption ùîº0‚Äã[(‚Äñ‚àáùêúha‚Äñ/ha)2]<‚àû\mathbb{E}\_{0}[(\|\nabla\_{\mathbf{c}}h\_{a}\|/h\_{a})^{2}]<\infty ensures this is well-defined.

Finally, the boundary term in ‚àácùí∞\nabla\_{c}\mathcal{U} involves the conditional mean ma‚Äã(r)m\_{a}(r) evaluated at the boundary surface. Since ma‚Äã(r)m\_{a}(r) is assumed to be continuous in rc‚Äão‚Äãn‚Äãtr\_{cont}, its value at the boundary is the limit of its values on the interior, which are identified from the observed data. This standard RDD-style argument ensures that ma‚Äã(r)m\_{a}(r) is identified for any rr at the boundary. This, together with the fact that hah\_{a} and œïa\phi\_{a} are known functions, guarantees that the entire boundary term is identified.
‚àé

## Appendix C Examples

This appendix applies the general framework developed in Appendix [B](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#A2 "Appendix B Derivation of the Marginal Policy Effect ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025. Wisse Rutgers acknowledges financial support from the Fundaci√≥n Ram√≥n Areces, the Maria de Maeztu Unit of Excellence CEX2020-001104-M, funded by MCIN/AEI/10.13039/501100011033, and CEMFI.") to the canonical examples presented in Section [4](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#S4 "4 Examples ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025. Wisse Rutgers acknowledges financial support from the Fundaci√≥n Ram√≥n Areces, the Maria de Maeztu Unit of Excellence CEX2020-001104-M, funded by MCIN/AEI/10.13039/501100011033, and CEMFI.") of the main text. For each example, we follow a three-step process: (1) we formally specify the model‚Äôs components, (2) we verify that the model satisfies the key assumptions required for our main theorem, and (3) we derive the specific form of the equilibrium-adjusted outcome, Œ®itotal\Psi\_{i}^{\text{total}}, by simplifying the general formula.

### C.1 Price-Based Allocation

#### C.1.1 Model Specification

The market allocates a single product (a‚àà{0,1}a\in\{0,1\}) with fixed supply q‚àà(0,1)q\in(0,1).

* ‚Ä¢

  Reports: Agents submit a continuous valuation Ri‚àà‚Ñù+R\_{i}\in\mathbb{R}\_{+}. We assume the baseline distribution of reports PR|0P\_{R|0} admits a continuous and positive density, fR‚Äã(r)f\_{R}(r).
* ‚Ä¢

  Allocation Rule: An agent receives the good if their report exceeds a market-clearing price or cutoff, c‚àà‚Ñù+c\in\mathbb{R}\_{+}. The allocation probability is thus:

  |  |  |  |
  | --- | --- | --- |
  |  | Œº1‚Äã(Ri,c)=ùüè‚Äã{Ri>c},Œº0‚Äã(Ri,c)=ùüè‚Äã{Ri‚â§c}.\mu\_{1}(R\_{i},c)=\mathbf{1}\{R\_{i}>c\},\quad\mu\_{0}(R\_{i},c)=\mathbf{1}\{R\_{i}\leq c\}. |  |
* ‚Ä¢

  Market Conduct Rule: The cutoff c0c\_{0} is set to satisfy the supply constraint, i.e., it is the (1‚àíq)(1-q)-quantile of the report distribution:

  |  |  |  |
  | --- | --- | --- |
  |  | ùîº0‚Äã[Œº1‚Äã(Ri,c0)]=‚à´c0‚àûfR‚Äã(r)‚Äãùëër=q.\mathbb{E}\_{0}[\mu\_{1}(R\_{i},c\_{0})]=\int\_{c\_{0}}^{\infty}f\_{R}(r)dr=q. |  |

#### C.1.2 Verification of Assumptions

We verify the key assumptions from Appendix [B](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#A2 "Appendix B Derivation of the Marginal Policy Effect ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025. Wisse Rutgers acknowledges financial support from the Fundaci√≥n Ram√≥n Areces, the Maria de Maeztu Unit of Excellence CEX2020-001104-M, funded by MCIN/AEI/10.13039/501100011033, and CEMFI.").

* ‚Ä¢

  Assumption [B.2](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#A2.Thmassumption2 "Assumption B.2 (Well-Behaved Mechanism). ‚Ä£ Appendix B Derivation of the Marginal Policy Effect ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025. Wisse Rutgers acknowledges financial support from the Fundaci√≥n Ram√≥n Areces, the Maria de Maeztu Unit of Excellence CEX2020-001104-M, funded by MCIN/AEI/10.13039/501100011033, and CEMFI.") (Well-Behaved Mechanism): The allocation rule fits the required decomposition. For a=1a=1, we have œï1‚Äã(Ri,c)=Ri‚àíc\phi\_{1}(R\_{i},c)=R\_{i}-c and h1‚Äã(Ri,c,PR)=1h\_{1}(R\_{i},c,P\_{R})=1. For a=0a=0, we have œï0‚Äã(Ri,c)=c‚àíRi\phi\_{0}(R\_{i},c)=c-R\_{i} and h0‚Äã(Ri,c,PR)=1h\_{0}(R\_{i},c,P\_{R})=1.

  1. 1.

     The functions ha=1h\_{a}=1 and œïa\phi\_{a} are continuously differentiable in cc.
  2. 2.

     The eligibility function œïa\phi\_{a} does not depend on PRP\_{R}.
  3. 3.

     The smooth component ha=1h\_{a}=1 is constant and thus trivially Hadamard differentiable in PRP\_{R}, with a derivative kernel La‚Äã(r,r‚Ä≤)=0L\_{a}(r,r^{\prime})=0.
  4. 4.

     All components are continuous.
* ‚Ä¢

  Assumption [B.1](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#A2.Thmassumption1 "Assumption B.1 (Marginal Agent Regularity). ‚Ä£ Appendix B Derivation of the Marginal Policy Effect ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025. Wisse Rutgers acknowledges financial support from the Fundaci√≥n Ram√≥n Areces, the Maria de Maeztu Unit of Excellence CEX2020-001104-M, funded by MCIN/AEI/10.13039/501100011033, and CEMFI.") (Marginal Agents): The report RiR\_{i} is fully continuous. We assume the conditional mean outcomes ma‚Äã(r)m\_{a}(r) are continuous in rr, as stated in the main text. The non-degeneracy condition ‚Äñ‚àárœïa‚Äñ2=|1|=1>0\|\nabla\_{r}\phi\_{a}\|\_{2}=|1|=1>0 holds.
* ‚Ä¢

  Assumption [B.3](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#A2.Thmassumption3 "Assumption B.3 (Differentiability of the Market Conduct Rule). ‚Ä£ Appendix B Derivation of the Marginal Policy Effect ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025. Wisse Rutgers acknowledges financial support from the Fundaci√≥n Ram√≥n Areces, the Maria de Maeztu Unit of Excellence CEX2020-001104-M, funded by MCIN/AEI/10.13039/501100011033, and CEMFI.") (Differentiability of Market Conduct): The market conduct rule is defined implicitly by G‚Äã(c,PR):=‚à´c‚àûùëëPR‚Äã(r)‚àíq=0G(c,P\_{R}):=\int\_{c}^{\infty}dP\_{R}(r)-q=0. This is differentiable in L2L\_{2}. By the Implicit Function Theorem, its derivative is c‚Ä≤‚Äã[sR]=‚àí(‚àÇG/‚àÇc)‚àí1‚Äã(‚àÇG/‚àÇPR)‚Äã[sR]c^{\prime}[s\_{R}]=-(\partial G/\partial c)^{-1}(\partial G/\partial P\_{R})[s\_{R}]. We have ‚àÇG/‚àÇc=‚àífR‚Äã(c)\partial G/\partial c=-f\_{R}(c) and (‚àÇG/‚àÇPR)‚Äã[sR]=ùîº0‚Äã[sR‚Äã(Ri)‚Äãùüè‚Äã{Ri>c}](\partial G/\partial P\_{R})[s\_{R}]=\mathbb{E}\_{0}[s\_{R}(R\_{i})\mathbf{1}\{R\_{i}>c\}]. Thus, c‚Ä≤‚Äã[sR]c^{\prime}[s\_{R}] is a continuous linear functional in L2L\_{2}, and the assumption holds.

Since the market conduct rule is differentiable in L2L\_{2}, Corollary [3.1](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#S3.Thmcorollary1 "Corollary 3.1 (The Equilibrium-Adjusted Outcome). ‚Ä£ 3.3 The Equilibrium-Adjusted Outcome ‚Ä£ 3 The Marginal Policy Effect ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025. Wisse Rutgers acknowledges financial support from the Fundaci√≥n Ram√≥n Areces, the Maria de Maeztu Unit of Excellence CEX2020-001104-M, funded by MCIN/AEI/10.13039/501100011033, and CEMFI.") applies.

#### C.1.3 Derivation of Œ®itotal\Psi\_{i}^{\text{total}}

We start with the general formula from Corollary [3.1](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#S3.Thmcorollary1 "Corollary 3.1 (The Equilibrium-Adjusted Outcome). ‚Ä£ 3.3 The Equilibrium-Adjusted Outcome ‚Ä£ 3 The Marginal Policy Effect ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025. Wisse Rutgers acknowledges financial support from the Fundaci√≥n Ram√≥n Areces, the Maria de Maeztu Unit of Excellence CEX2020-001104-M, funded by MCIN/AEI/10.13039/501100011033, and CEMFI."): Œ®itotal=Œ®ifixed+Œ®conduct‚Äã(Ri)\Psi\_{i}^{\text{total}}=\Psi\_{i}^{\text{fixed}}+\Psi^{\text{conduct}}(R\_{i}).

1. 1.

   Fixed Component Œ®ifixed=Yi+Œ≥‚Äã(Ri)\Psi\_{i}^{\text{fixed}}=Y\_{i}+\gamma(R\_{i}):
   The competition externality, Œ≥‚Äã(Ri)\gamma(R\_{i}), depends on the kernel LaL\_{a}. Since hah\_{a} is constant with respect to PRP\_{R}, its derivative kernel La‚Äã(r,r‚Ä≤)L\_{a}(r,r^{\prime}) is identically zero. Therefore, Œ≥‚Äã(Ri)=0\gamma(R\_{i})=0, and Œ®ifixed=Yi\Psi\_{i}^{\text{fixed}}=Y\_{i}.
2. 2.

   Market Conduct Component Œ®conduct‚Äã(Ri)=‚àácùí∞‚Äã(c0)‚ãÖœàc0‚Äã(Ri)\Psi^{\text{conduct}}(R\_{i})=\nabla\_{c}\mathcal{U}(c\_{0})\cdot\psi\_{c\_{0}}(R\_{i}):
   We need to derive the welfare gradient ‚àácùí∞‚Äã(c0)\nabla\_{c}\mathcal{U}(c\_{0}) and the influence function of the cutoff, œàc0‚Äã(Ri)\psi\_{c\_{0}}(R\_{i}).

   * ‚Ä¢

     Welfare Gradient ‚àácùí∞‚Äã(c0)\nabla\_{c}\mathcal{U}(c\_{0}): We apply Theorem [A.1](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#A1.Thmtheorem1 "Theorem A.1. ‚Ä£ Appendix A Differentiating integrals ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025. Wisse Rutgers acknowledges financial support from the Fundaci√≥n Ram√≥n Areces, the Maria de Maeztu Unit of Excellence CEX2020-001104-M, funded by MCIN/AEI/10.13039/501100011033, and CEMFI."). Since ha=1h\_{a}=1 does not depend on cc, the volume term is zero. The derivative comes entirely from the boundary term. For a=1a=1, the boundary is at Ri=cR\_{i}=c, and for a=0a=0, it is also at Ri=cR\_{i}=c. A marginal increase in cc moves agents from allocation 1 to 0. The total effect is the mass of agents at the boundary, fR‚Äã(c0)f\_{R}(c\_{0}), times their change in average outcome, m0‚Äã(c0)‚àím1‚Äã(c0)m\_{0}(c\_{0})-m\_{1}(c\_{0}).

     |  |  |  |
     | --- | --- | --- |
     |  | ‚àácùí∞‚Äã(c0)=‚àí[m1‚Äã(c0)‚àím0‚Äã(c0)]‚ÄãfR‚Äã(c0)=‚àíœÑ‚Äã(c0)‚ÄãfR‚Äã(c0).\nabla\_{c}\mathcal{U}(c\_{0})=-[m\_{1}(c\_{0})-m\_{0}(c\_{0})]f\_{R}(c\_{0})=-\tau(c\_{0})f\_{R}(c\_{0}). |  |
   * ‚Ä¢

     Influence Function œàc0‚Äã(Ri)\psi\_{c\_{0}}(R\_{i}): From the verification of Assumption [B.3](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#A2.Thmassumption3 "Assumption B.3 (Differentiability of the Market Conduct Rule). ‚Ä£ Appendix B Derivation of the Marginal Policy Effect ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025. Wisse Rutgers acknowledges financial support from the Fundaci√≥n Ram√≥n Areces, the Maria de Maeztu Unit of Excellence CEX2020-001104-M, funded by MCIN/AEI/10.13039/501100011033, and CEMFI."), we have c‚Ä≤‚Äã[sR]=ùîº0‚Äã[sR‚Äã(Ri)‚Äãùüè‚Äã{Ri>c0}fR‚Äã(c0)]c^{\prime}[s\_{R}]=\mathbb{E}\_{0}[s\_{R}(R\_{i})\frac{\mathbf{1}\{R\_{i}>c\_{0}\}}{f\_{R}(c\_{0})}]. By definition, the influence function is the term inside the expectation multiplying the score:

     |  |  |  |
     | --- | --- | --- |
     |  | œàc0‚Äã(Ri)=ùüè‚Äã{Ri>c0}fR‚Äã(c0)=AifR‚Äã(c0).\psi\_{c\_{0}}(R\_{i})=\frac{\mathbf{1}\{R\_{i}>c\_{0}\}}{f\_{R}(c\_{0})}=\frac{A\_{i}}{f\_{R}(c\_{0})}. |  |

   Combining these pieces, the market conduct externality is:

   |  |  |  |  |
   | --- | --- | --- | --- |
   |  | Œ®conduct‚Äã(Ri)\displaystyle\Psi^{\text{conduct}}(R\_{i}) | =‚àácùí∞‚Äã(c0)‚ãÖœàc0‚Äã(Ri)\displaystyle=\nabla\_{c}\mathcal{U}(c\_{0})\cdot\psi\_{c\_{0}}(R\_{i}) |  |
   |  |  |  |  |
   | --- | --- | --- | --- |
   |  |  | =(‚àíœÑ‚Äã(c0)‚ÄãfR‚Äã(c0))‚ãÖ(AifR‚Äã(c0))=‚àíœÑ‚Äã(c0)‚ÄãAi.\displaystyle=\left(-\tau(c\_{0})f\_{R}(c\_{0})\right)\cdot\left(\frac{A\_{i}}{f\_{R}(c\_{0})}\right)=-\tau(c\_{0})A\_{i}. |  |
3. 3.

   Total Equilibrium-Adjusted Outcome:
   Summing the components gives the final result:

   |  |  |  |
   | --- | --- | --- |
   |  | Œ®itotal=Yi‚àíœÑ‚Äã(c0)‚ÄãAi.\Psi\_{i}^{\text{total}}=Y\_{i}-\tau(c\_{0})A\_{i}. |  |

   This matches the expression in the main text. The density terms fR‚Äã(c0)f\_{R}(c\_{0}) cancel out, revealing that the externality an inframarginal agent imposes by taking a slot is exactly the welfare loss of the single marginal agent they displace.

### C.2 School Choice with Multiple Schools

#### C.2.1 Model Specification

We consider a market with two schools (k‚àà{1,2}k\in\{1,2\}) and an outside option (a=0a=0). Each school has a fixed capacity qkq\_{k}.

* ‚Ä¢

  Reports: An agent‚Äôs report is a vector Ri=(‚âªi,Vi,1,Vi,2)R\_{i}=(\succ\_{i},V\_{i,1},V\_{i,2}), consisting of a strict preference ranking ‚âªi\succ\_{i} over {0,1,2}\{0,1,2\} and a vector of school-specific continuous scores (e.g., grades or test scores).
* ‚Ä¢

  Allocation Rule: The market is cleared by a vector of score cutoffs ùêú=(c1,c2)\mathbf{c}=(c\_{1},c\_{2}). An agent is eligible for school kk if their score exceeds the cutoff, Vi,k>ckV\_{i,k}>c\_{k}. Each agent is assigned to their most-preferred school for which they are eligible. If they are not eligible for any school they prefer to the outside option, they receive a=0a=0.
* ‚Ä¢

  Market Conduct Rule: The cutoff vector ùêú0\mathbf{c}\_{0} is determined by the system of capacity constraints:

  |  |  |  |  |
  | --- | --- | --- | --- |
  |  | ùîº0‚Äã[Œº1‚Äã(Ri,ùêú0)]\displaystyle\mathbb{E}\_{0}[\mu\_{1}(R\_{i},\mathbf{c}\_{0})] | =q1\displaystyle=q\_{1} |  |
  |  |  |  |  |
  | --- | --- | --- | --- |
  |  | ùîº0‚Äã[Œº2‚Äã(Ri,ùêú0)]\displaystyle\mathbb{E}\_{0}[\mu\_{2}(R\_{i},\mathbf{c}\_{0})] | =q2\displaystyle=q\_{2} |  |

#### C.2.2 Verification of Assumptions

* ‚Ä¢

  Assumption [B.2](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#A2.Thmassumption2 "Assumption B.2 (Well-Behaved Mechanism). ‚Ä£ Appendix B Derivation of the Marginal Policy Effect ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025. Wisse Rutgers acknowledges financial support from the Fundaci√≥n Ram√≥n Areces, the Maria de Maeztu Unit of Excellence CEX2020-001104-M, funded by MCIN/AEI/10.13039/501100011033, and CEMFI.") (Well-Behaved Mechanism): For any given preference ranking ‚âªi\succ\_{i}, the allocation rule is a series of indicator functions based on the scores. For example, for an agent with preferences 1‚âª2‚âª01\succ\_{2}\succ 0, the allocation rule is Œº1‚Äã(Ri,ùêú)=ùüè‚Äã{Vi,1>c1}\mu\_{1}(R\_{i},\mathbf{c})=\mathbf{1}\{V\_{i,1}>c\_{1}\} and Œº2‚Äã(Ri,ùêú)=ùüè‚Äã{Vi,1‚â§c1,Vi,2>c2}\mu\_{2}(R\_{i},\mathbf{c})=\mathbf{1}\{V\_{i,1}\leq c\_{1},V\_{i,2}>c\_{2}\}. Each of these can be written in the required form with ha=1h\_{a}=1 and œïa\phi\_{a} being a function of the score margins (e.g., œï1=Vi,1‚àíc1\phi\_{1}=V\_{i,1}-c\_{1}). The conditions on smoothness, anonymity, and Hadamard differentiability (with La=0L\_{a}=0) hold trivially.
* ‚Ä¢

  Assumption [B.1](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#A2.Thmassumption1 "Assumption B.1 (Marginal Agent Regularity). ‚Ä£ Appendix B Derivation of the Marginal Policy Effect ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025. Wisse Rutgers acknowledges financial support from the Fundaci√≥n Ram√≥n Areces, the Maria de Maeztu Unit of Excellence CEX2020-001104-M, funded by MCIN/AEI/10.13039/501100011033, and CEMFI.") (Marginal Agents): The scores (Vi,1,Vi,2)(V\_{i,1},V\_{i,2}) are the continuous components of the report, while the preference ranking ‚âªi\succ\_{i} is the discrete component. We assume ma‚Äã(Ri)m\_{a}(R\_{i}) is continuous in the scores. The non-degeneracy condition on the gradients of œïa\phi\_{a} holds.
* ‚Ä¢

  Assumption [B.3](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#A2.Thmassumption3 "Assumption B.3 (Differentiability of the Market Conduct Rule). ‚Ä£ Appendix B Derivation of the Marginal Policy Effect ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025. Wisse Rutgers acknowledges financial support from the Fundaci√≥n Ram√≥n Areces, the Maria de Maeztu Unit of Excellence CEX2020-001104-M, funded by MCIN/AEI/10.13039/501100011033, and CEMFI.") (Differentiability of Market Conduct): The market conduct rule is defined by the system of equations ùêÜ‚Äã(ùêú,PR):=ùîºPR‚Äã[ùùÅ‚Äã(Ri,ùêú)]‚àíùê™=ùüé\mathbf{G}(\mathbf{c},P\_{R}):=\mathbb{E}\_{P\_{R}}[\bm{\mu}(R\_{i},\mathbf{c})]-\mathbf{q}=\mathbf{0}. The Jacobian of this system is Jk‚Äãj=‚àÇGk/‚àÇcjJ\_{kj}=\partial G\_{k}/\partial c\_{j}. We assume this matrix is invertible at ùêú0\mathbf{c}\_{0}, which requires that the cross-school substitution effects are not perfectly collinear. The rule is differentiable in L2L\_{2}.

As in the previous example, Corollary [3.1](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#S3.Thmcorollary1 "Corollary 3.1 (The Equilibrium-Adjusted Outcome). ‚Ä£ 3.3 The Equilibrium-Adjusted Outcome ‚Ä£ 3 The Marginal Policy Effect ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025. Wisse Rutgers acknowledges financial support from the Fundaci√≥n Ram√≥n Areces, the Maria de Maeztu Unit of Excellence CEX2020-001104-M, funded by MCIN/AEI/10.13039/501100011033, and CEMFI.") applies.

#### C.2.3 Derivation of Œ®itotal\Psi\_{i}^{\text{total}}

We again use the formula Œ®itotal=Yi+Œ≥‚Äã(Ri)+Œ®conduct‚Äã(Ri)\Psi\_{i}^{\text{total}}=Y\_{i}+\gamma(R\_{i})+\Psi^{\text{conduct}}(R\_{i}).

1. 1.

   Fixed Component Œ®ifixed\Psi\_{i}^{\text{fixed}}: Since the allocation rule (conditional on preferences) does not depend on PRP\_{R}, the derivative kernel LaL\_{a} is zero. This implies the competition externality is Œ≥‚Äã(Ri)=0\gamma(R\_{i})=0, and thus Œ®ifixed=Yi\Psi\_{i}^{\text{fixed}}=Y\_{i}.
2. 2.

   Market Conduct Component Œ®conduct‚Äã(Ri)\Psi^{\text{conduct}}(R\_{i}): This component is given by ‚ü®‚àáùêúùí∞‚Äã(ùêú0),ùùçùêú0‚Äã(Ri)‚ü©\langle\nabla\_{\mathbf{c}}\mathcal{U}(\mathbf{c}\_{0}),\bm{\psi}\_{\mathbf{c}\_{0}}(R\_{i})\rangle, where the gradient and influence function are now vectors.

   * ‚Ä¢

     Influence Function œàùêú0‚Äã(Ri)\bm{\psi}\_{\mathbf{c}\_{0}}(R\_{i}): Applying the Implicit Function Theorem to the vector market conduct rule gives ùêú‚Ä≤‚Äã[sR]=‚àíJ0‚àí1‚Äã(‚àÇùêÜ/‚àÇPR)‚Äã[sR]\mathbf{c}^{\prime}[s\_{R}]=-J\_{0}^{-1}(\partial\mathbf{G}/\partial P\_{R})[s\_{R}]. The second term is ùîº0‚Äã[sR‚Äã(Ri)‚ÄãùùÅ‚Äã(Ri,ùêú0)]=ùîº0‚Äã[sR‚Äã(Ri)‚ÄãùêÄi]\mathbb{E}\_{0}[s\_{R}(R\_{i})\bm{\mu}(R\_{i},\mathbf{c}\_{0})]=\mathbb{E}\_{0}[s\_{R}(R\_{i})\mathbf{A}\_{i}], where ùêÄi\mathbf{A}\_{i} is the vector of allocation indicators. The vector-valued influence function is therefore:

     |  |  |  |
     | --- | --- | --- |
     |  | ùùçùêú0‚Äã(Ri)=‚àíJ0‚àí1‚ÄãùêÄi.\bm{\psi}\_{\mathbf{c}\_{0}}(R\_{i})=-J\_{0}^{-1}\mathbf{A}\_{i}. |  |
   * ‚Ä¢

     Welfare Gradient ‚àáùêúùí∞‚Äã(ùêú0)\nabla\_{\mathbf{c}}\mathcal{U}(\mathbf{c}\_{0}): We apply Theorem [A.1](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#A1.Thmtheorem1 "Theorem A.1. ‚Ä£ Appendix A Differentiating integrals ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025. Wisse Rutgers acknowledges financial support from the Fundaci√≥n Ram√≥n Areces, the Maria de Maeztu Unit of Excellence CEX2020-001104-M, funded by MCIN/AEI/10.13039/501100011033, and CEMFI."). The derivative with respect to a single cutoff, cjc\_{j}, is determined by the welfare change of agents at that margin (Vi,j=cjV\_{i,j}=c\_{j}). Let œÅj‚Üík\rho\_{j\to k} be the density of agents with score Vi,j=cjV\_{i,j}=c\_{j} who, upon losing eligibility for school jj, are reallocated to their next-best option, kk. Let œÑj‚Üík‚Äã(cj)\tau\_{j\to k}(c\_{j}) be their average change in outcome. The jj-th component of the gradient is the sum over all possible reallocations from margin jj:

     |  |  |  |
     | --- | --- | --- |
     |  | ‚àÇùí∞‚àÇcj‚Äã(ùêú0)=‚àí‚àëk‚ààùíúœÅj‚Üík‚ÄãœÑj‚Üík‚Äã(cj).\frac{\partial\mathcal{U}}{\partial c\_{j}}(\mathbf{c}\_{0})=-\sum\_{k\in\mathcal{A}}\rho\_{j\to k}\tau\_{j\to k}(c\_{j}). |  |

     This corresponds to the vector ùùà~\tilde{\bm{\sigma}} defined in the main text.
   * ‚Ä¢

     The Jacobian Matrix J0J\_{0}: The entry Jk‚Äãj=‚àÇùîº0‚Äã[Œºk]/‚àÇcjJ\_{kj}=\partial\mathbb{E}\_{0}[\mu\_{k}]/\partial c\_{j} measures how enrollment at school kk changes when the cutoff for school jj increases. The diagonal elements Jj‚ÄãjJ\_{jj} are negative (enrollment at jj falls). The off-diagonal elements Jk‚ÄãjJ\_{kj} (k‚â†jk\neq j) are positive and represent the substitution effects: the density of agents who are pushed out of school jj and into school kk, i.e., Jk‚Äãj=œÅj‚ÜíkJ\_{kj}=\rho\_{j\to k}.

   Combining these, the market conduct externality is:

   |  |  |  |  |
   | --- | --- | --- | --- |
   |  | Œ®conduct‚Äã(Ri)\displaystyle\Psi^{\text{conduct}}(R\_{i}) | =‚ü®‚àáùêúùí∞‚Äã(ùêú0),ùùçùêú0‚Äã(Ri)‚ü©=(‚àáùêúùí∞‚Äã(ùêú0))‚ä§‚Äã(‚àíJ0‚àí1‚ÄãùêÄi)\displaystyle=\langle\nabla\_{\mathbf{c}}\mathcal{U}(\mathbf{c}\_{0}),\bm{\psi}\_{\mathbf{c}\_{0}}(R\_{i})\rangle=(\nabla\_{\mathbf{c}}\mathcal{U}(\mathbf{c}\_{0}))^{\top}(-J\_{0}^{-1}\mathbf{A}\_{i}) |  |
   |  |  |  |  |
   | --- | --- | --- | --- |
   |  |  | =‚àí((J0‚àí1)‚ä§‚Äã‚àáùêúùí∞‚Äã(ùêú0))‚ä§‚ÄãùêÄi.\displaystyle=-\left((J\_{0}^{-1})^{\top}\nabla\_{\mathbf{c}}\mathcal{U}(\mathbf{c}\_{0})\right)^{\top}\mathbf{A}\_{i}. |  |

   Let us define the vector of social externality values ùêØ:=(J0‚àí1)‚ä§‚Äã‚àáùêúùí∞‚Äã(ùêú0)\mathbf{v}:=(J\_{0}^{-1})^{\top}\nabla\_{\mathbf{c}}\mathcal{U}(\mathbf{c}\_{0}). Then the expression simplifies to Œ®conduct‚Äã(Ri)=‚àíùêØ‚ä§‚ÄãùêÄi\Psi^{\text{conduct}}(R\_{i})=-\mathbf{v}^{\top}\mathbf{A}\_{i}.
3. 3.

   Total Equilibrium-Adjusted Outcome:
   Summing the components gives the final vector form:

   |  |  |  |
   | --- | --- | --- |
   |  | Œ®itotal=Yi‚àíùêØ‚ä§‚ÄãùêÄi=Yi‚àív1‚ãÖùüè‚Äã{Ai=1}‚àív2‚ãÖùüè‚Äã{Ai=2}.\Psi\_{i}^{\text{total}}=Y\_{i}-\mathbf{v}^{\top}\mathbf{A}\_{i}=Y\_{i}-v\_{1}\cdot\mathbf{1}\{A\_{i}=1\}-v\_{2}\cdot\mathbf{1}\{A\_{i}=2\}. |  |

   This result shows that the social value of a seat at a given school, vkv\_{k}, is a complex combination of the marginal treatment effects at \*all\* cutoffs, weighted by the full matrix of equilibrium substitution patterns captured by (J0‚àí1)‚ä§(J\_{0}^{-1})^{\top}.

### C.3 Second-Price Auction with a Reserve Price

#### C.3.1 Model Specification

We consider a sealed-bid, second-price auction for a single good (a‚àà{0,1}a\in\{0,1\}) among nn i.i.d. participants.

* ‚Ä¢

  Reports: Each agent ii submits a bid Ri‚àà‚Ñù+R\_{i}\in\mathbb{R}\_{+}, which we take to be their private valuation.
* ‚Ä¢

  Allocation Rule: An agent wins if their bid is above the reserve price, cc, and is the highest of all nn bids. The probability of winning is Œº1‚Äã(r,c,PR)=ùüè‚Äã{r>c}‚ãÖFR‚Äã(r)n‚àí1\mu\_{1}(r,c,P\_{R})=\mathbf{1}\{r>c\}\cdot F\_{R}(r)^{n-1}.
* ‚Ä¢

  Market Conduct Rule: The reserve price c0c\_{0} is set to ensure the ex-ante probability of an agent winning is a fixed quantity qq. This rule simplifies to an algebraic equation:

  |  |  |  |
  | --- | --- | --- |
  |  | 1n‚Äã(1‚àíFR|0‚Äã(c0)n)=q.\displaystyle\frac{1}{n}\left(1-F\_{R|0}(c\_{0})^{n}\right)=q. |  |

#### C.3.2 Derivation of Œ®itotal\Psi\_{i}^{\text{total}}

The total equilibrium-adjusted outcome is the sum of the private outcome and two distinct externality terms: Œ®itotal=Yi+Œ≥‚Äã(Ri)+Œ®conduct‚Äã(Ri)\Psi\_{i}^{\text{total}}=Y\_{i}+\gamma(R\_{i})+\Psi^{\text{conduct}}(R\_{i}).

##### 1. Competition Externality Œ≥‚Äã(Ri)\gamma(R\_{i}):

This term captures the welfare impact from a change in the bid distribution on other bidders, holding the reserve price fixed. It simplifies to an intuitive expression involving the maximum order statistic of the n‚àí1n-1 competing bids, which we denote R(n‚àí1)R\_{(n-1)}:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | Œ≥‚Äã(Ri)=ùîº0‚Äã[œÑ‚Äã(R(n‚àí1))|R(n‚àí1)‚â•r~]√ó(1‚àíFR|0‚Äã(r~)n‚àí1),where¬†‚Äãr~=max‚Å°(c0,Ri).\displaystyle\gamma(R\_{i})=\mathbb{E}\_{0}\left[\tau(R\_{(n-1)})|R\_{(n-1)}\geq\tilde{r}\right]\times\left(1-F\_{R|0}(\tilde{r})^{n-1}\right),\qquad\text{where }\tilde{r}=\max(c\_{0},R\_{i}). |  |

This is the expected treatment effect for the winning competitor, conditional on them being a relevant threat (bidding above r~\tilde{r}), multiplied by the probability that such a threat exists.

##### 2. Market Conduct Externality Œ®conduct‚Äã(Ri)\Psi^{\text{conduct}}(R\_{i}):

This term captures the welfare impact from agent ii‚Äôs influence on the equilibrium reserve price. We derive its influence function, œàc0‚Äã(Ri)\psi\_{c\_{0}}(R\_{i}), from the simplified market conduct rule using the Implicit Function Theorem. This yields:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | œàc0‚Äã(Ri)=ùüè‚Äã{Ri>c0}fR|0‚Äã(c0).\displaystyle\psi\_{c\_{0}}(R\_{i})=\frac{\mathbf{1}\{R\_{i}>c\_{0}\}}{f\_{R|0}(c\_{0})}. |  |

Multiplying this by the welfare gradient, ‚àácùí∞‚Äã(c0)=‚àíœÑ‚Äã(c0)‚ÄãFR|0‚Äã(c0)n‚àí1‚ÄãfR|0‚Äã(c0)\nabla\_{c}\mathcal{U}(c\_{0})=-\tau(c\_{0})F\_{R|0}(c\_{0})^{n-1}f\_{R|0}(c\_{0}), gives the externality:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | Œ®conduct‚Äã(Ri)=‚àíœÑ‚Äã(c0)‚ÄãFR|0‚Äã(c0)n‚àí1‚ãÖùüè‚Äã{Ri>c0}.\displaystyle\Psi^{\text{conduct}}(R\_{i})=-\tau(c\_{0})F\_{R|0}(c\_{0})^{n-1}\cdot\mathbf{1}\{R\_{i}>c\_{0}\}. |  |

This shows the externality is non-zero only for losing bidders.

### C.4 Auction with an Optimal Reserve Price

We now modify the previous auction example by changing the platform‚Äôs objective. Instead of setting a reserve price to meet a quantity target, the platform sets it to maximize expected revenue, following Myerson (1981).

#### C.4.1 Model Specification

The setup for agents, reports, and the allocation rule is identical to the second-price auction in the previous section. The only change is the market conduct rule.

* ‚Ä¢

  Market Conduct Rule: The reserve price cc is set to solve the platform‚Äôs first-order condition for revenue maximization:

  |  |  |  |
  | --- | --- | --- |
  |  | G‚Äã(c,PR):=(1‚àíFR‚Äã(c))‚àíc‚ÄãfR‚Äã(c)=0,G(c,P\_{R}):=(1-F\_{R}(c))-cf\_{R}(c)=0, |  |

  where fR‚Äã(c)f\_{R}(c) is the probability density function of reports evaluated at the reserve price cc.

#### C.4.2 Verification of Assumptions

The presence of the density term fR‚Äã(c)f\_{R}(c) in the market conduct rule makes its differentiability properties more subtle.

* ‚Ä¢

  Failure in L2L\_{2}: The derivative of the functional c‚Äã(PR)c(P\_{R}) with respect to a perturbation with score sRs\_{R} can be found via the Implicit Function Theorem. This derivative involves a term proportional to fR‚Äã(c0)‚ÄãsR‚Äã(c0)f\_{R}(c\_{0})s\_{R}(c\_{0}), which is a point evaluation of the score function. The point-evaluation operator is not a continuous linear functional on the space L2‚Äã(Ri)L\_{2}(R\_{i}). A sequence of scores can converge to zero in the L2L\_{2} norm while diverging at the specific point c0c\_{0}. Consequently, Assumption [B.3](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#A2.Thmassumption3 "Assumption B.3 (Differentiability of the Market Conduct Rule). ‚Ä£ Appendix B Derivation of the Marginal Policy Effect ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025. Wisse Rutgers acknowledges financial support from the Fundaci√≥n Ram√≥n Areces, the Maria de Maeztu Unit of Excellence CEX2020-001104-M, funded by MCIN/AEI/10.13039/501100011033, and CEMFI.") is violated for the standard L2L\_{2} space, and Corollary [3.1](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#S3.Thmcorollary1 "Corollary 3.1 (The Equilibrium-Adjusted Outcome). ‚Ä£ 3.3 The Equilibrium-Adjusted Outcome ‚Ä£ 3 The Marginal Policy Effect ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025. Wisse Rutgers acknowledges financial support from the Fundaci√≥n Ram√≥n Areces, the Maria de Maeztu Unit of Excellence CEX2020-001104-M, funded by MCIN/AEI/10.13039/501100011033, and CEMFI.") does not apply.
* ‚Ä¢

  Resolution in Sobolev Space: To proceed, we must restrict the class of admissible policy reforms to those that induce sufficiently smooth scores. We assume the space of report scores ‚ÑãR\mathcal{H}\_{R} is a weighted Sobolev space H1H^{1}, with the inner product:

  |  |  |  |
  | --- | --- | --- |
  |  | ‚ü®œà,s‚ü©H1:=ùîº0‚Äã[œà‚Äã(Ri)‚Äãs‚Äã(Ri)]+ùîº0‚Äã[œà‚Ä≤‚Äã(Ri)‚Äãs‚Ä≤‚Äã(Ri)].\langle\psi,s\rangle\_{H^{1}}:=\mathbb{E}\_{0}[\psi(R\_{i})s(R\_{i})]+\mathbb{E}\_{0}[\psi^{\prime}(R\_{i})s^{\prime}(R\_{i})]. |  |

  In this space, the Sobolev embedding theorem ensures that point evaluation is a continuous operator. Therefore, the functional c‚Äã(PR)c(P\_{R}) is continuously differentiable. Assumption [B.3](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#A2.Thmassumption3 "Assumption B.3 (Differentiability of the Market Conduct Rule). ‚Ä£ Appendix B Derivation of the Marginal Policy Effect ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025. Wisse Rutgers acknowledges financial support from the Fundaci√≥n Ram√≥n Areces, the Maria de Maeztu Unit of Excellence CEX2020-001104-M, funded by MCIN/AEI/10.13039/501100011033, and CEMFI.") now holds, but for this stronger Hilbert space. All other assumptions are maintained as before.

#### C.4.3 Derivation of the MPE

Since Corollary [3.1](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#S3.Thmcorollary1 "Corollary 3.1 (The Equilibrium-Adjusted Outcome). ‚Ä£ 3.3 The Equilibrium-Adjusted Outcome ‚Ä£ 3 The Marginal Policy Effect ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025. Wisse Rutgers acknowledges financial support from the Fundaci√≥n Ram√≥n Areces, the Maria de Maeztu Unit of Excellence CEX2020-001104-M, funded by MCIN/AEI/10.13039/501100011033, and CEMFI.") does not apply, we must use the general form of the MPE from Theorem [3.1](https://arxiv.org/html/2510.20032v1#S3.Thmtheorem1 "Theorem 3.1 (The Marginal Policy Effect). ‚Ä£ 3.3 The Equilibrium-Adjusted Outcome ‚Ä£ 3 The Marginal Policy Effect ‚Ä£ Evaluating Local Policies in Centralized MarketsWe thank Kevin Chen, Ramesh Johari, Lihua Lei, Evan Munro, Davide Viviano, and Stefan Wager for their feedback, which has greatly improved the paper. We also thank seminar participants at Harvard and Stanford, as well as conference participants at the 2024 Winter Meetings of the Econometric Society, and ACIC 2025.
